{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01YW6h3Hyf4fk93b1nnhUEXk","type":"tool_result","content":[{"type":"text","text":"{\"number\":1,\"title\":\"fix: add @lid format support and allowFrom wildcard handling\",\"body\":\"## Summary\\n\\nThis PR fixes two critical bugs that prevent the web relay from processing inbound messages on newer WhatsApp versions:\\n\\n1. **LID format not recognized**: WhatsApp now uses Linked ID (`@lid`) format for message senders instead of the traditional `@s.whatsapp.net` format. The current `jidToE164()` function silently drops these messages.\\n\\n2. **Wildcard `\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;` in allowFrom doesn\\u0026#39;t work**: The `allowFrom: [\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;]` configuration is documented to allow all senders, but the code performs an exact string match, so `\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;` never matches any phone number.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Bug 1: LID Format Not Supported\\n\\n### Problem\\n\\nWhatsApp has transitioned to using Linked IDs (LID) for identifying users in newer API versions. Messages now arrive with JIDs in the format:\\n\\n```\\n142326760485098@lid\\n```\\n\\nInstead of the traditional format:\\n\\n```\\n5561983297558@s.whatsapp.net\\n```\\n\\nThe current `jidToE164()` function in `src/utils.ts` only matches the `@s.whatsapp.net` format, causing all inbound messages from `@lid` JIDs to be silently dropped.\\n\\n### Solution\\n\\nUpdated `jidToE164()` to check for `@lid` format and use the existing reverse mapping files that warelay already creates in `~/.warelay/credentials/lid-mapping-*_reverse.json`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Bug 2: allowFrom Wildcard Not Working\\n\\n### Problem\\n\\nThe `allowFrom` configuration is documented to support `\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;` as a wildcard to allow messages from all senders. However, the implementation performs an exact string match:\\n\\n```typescript\\nif (!allowFrom.includes(from)) {  // Exact match only!\\n```\\n\\nWhen `allowFrom: [\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;]` is configured, the check fails because `\\u0026#34;+556183297558\\u0026#34;` is not literally in `[\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;]`.\\n\\n### Solution\\n\\nAdded a check for the wildcard before performing the exact match:\\n\\n```typescript\\nif (!allowFrom.includes(\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;) \\u0026amp;\\u0026amp; !allowFrom.includes(from)) {\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\n1. **LID Format Resolution**: Messages from `@lid` JIDs are now correctly resolved to E.164 phone numbers\\n2. **allowFrom Wildcard**: `allowFrom: [\\u0026#34;*\\u0026#34;]` now correctly allows all senders\\n3. **Backward Compatibility**: Traditional `@s.whatsapp.net` JIDs and explicit phone number lists continue to work\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Files Changed\\n\\n| File | Change |\\n|------|--------|\\n| `src/utils.ts` | Add `@lid` format support to `jidToE164()` |\\n| `src/auto-reply/reply.ts` | Add wildcard check in `allowFrom` validation |\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Breaking Changes\\n\\nNone. There is no configuration path to opt into private network access, even in explicitly local gateway deployments where SSRF risk is not a concern.\\n\\n### Proposed solution\\n\\nIntroduce an `allowPrivateNetwork` boolean option for `web_fetch`, `web_search`, and `image_tool`. When running in `local` gateway mode, automatically set `allowPrivateNetwork: true` for a seamless local-first experience. Wire this flag through the SSRF guard (`fetchWithSsrFGuard`) so that private addresses are reachable when the option is enabled.\\n\\n### Alternatives considered\\n\\nManually whitelisting specific IPs in the SSRF guard — too brittle and requires code changes per deployment. Routing local services through a public proxy — adds unnecessary latency and defeats the purpose of self-hosting.\\n\\n### Impact\\n\\n- **Affected:** Teams running self-hosted search engines (SearXNG, etc.) or air-gapped/private deployments\\n- **Severity:** Blocks workflow — private network access is completely unavailable today\\n- **Frequency:** Always, for any private-network deployment\\n- **Consequence:** Self-hosted search is non-functional; operators must use cloud search providers even when a local alternative exists\\n\\n### Evidence/examples\\n\\n- SearXNG Docker backward-compatible: `allowPrivateNetwork` defaults to `false`, preserving existing SSRF protection for all non-local deployments\\n- A troubleshooting guide for plaintext WebSocket/HTTP issues on gateway probe fail in environments where:\\nthe gateway is healthy\\nnormal RPC calls succeed\\nbut the probe path is slightly slower than 800ms\\nThat creates a misleading state like a bug**\\nBecause the CLI currently presents --timeout as a probe-wide timeout budget, but the implementation hard-limits localLoopback to 800ms regardless of that value.\\n\\nThis makes gateway Anthropic setup-token silently truncated when terminal line-wraps during paste\",\"body\":\"### Bug type\\n\\nRegression (worked before, now fails)\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\n`claude setup-token` generates 108-character OAuth tokens. When pasted into OpenClaw's Clack text prompts (`openclaw models auth` or `openclaw models auth paste-token`), the token wraps across two terminal lines and only the first ~80 characters are captured. The truncated token passes validation (`ANTHROPIC_SETUP_TOKEN_MIN_LENGTH` is 80) and gets stored in `auth-profiles.json`, but every Anthropic API call fails with `401 Invalid bearer token`. There is no indication the token was truncated.\\n\\n### Steps to reproduce\\n\\n1. Run `claude setup-token` in terminal — generates a 108-character `sk-ant-oat01-*` token\\n2. Run `openclaw models auth` and select Anthropic setup-token flow\\n3. Paste the token into the Clack text prompt — token wraps across two lines in terminal\\n4. Only the first ~80 characters are captured and stored in `auth-profiles.json`\\n5. All Anthropic API calls fail with `401 authentication_error: Invalid bearer token`\\n\\n### Expected behavior\\n\\nThe full 108-character token should be stored. Token input should strip newline/carriage-return characters that occur when the terminal wraps long tokens across multiple lines.\\n\\nSuggested fix: replace `.trim()` with `.replace(/[\\\\n\\\\r\\\\s]+/g, \\\"\\\").trim()` in the token input handlers in:\\n- `dist/extensions/anthropic/index.js` (line 323)\\n- `dist/models-C6Rr59E2.js` (line 358)\\n- `dist/pi-embedded-CzQCqSlH.js` `validateAnthropicSetupToken` (line 10961)\\n\\n### Actual behavior\\n\\nOnly the first ~80 characters of the 108-character setup-token are stored in `auth-profiles.json`. The truncated token passes validation but every Anthropic API call returns `401 authentication_error: Invalid bearer token`. The gateway logs show auth failures on all Anthropic models with no indication that the token was truncated during input.\\n\\n### OpenClaw version\\n\\n2026.3.22\\n\\n### Operating system\\n\\nmacOS 14.3 (Darwin 23.3.0)\\n\\n### Install method\\n\\nnpm global\\n\\n### Model\\n\\nanthropic/claude-opus-4-6, anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6\\n\\n### Provider / routing chain\\n\\nopenclaw -\\u003e anthropic (direct, setup-token auth)\\n\\n### Additional provider/model setup details\\n\\nAuth profile stored in `~/.openclaw/agents/main/agent/auth-profiles.json` as `type: \\\"token\\\"` with provider `anthropic`. Token generated via `claude setup-token` (Claude Code v2.1.78). The Clack text prompt captures only the first terminal line (~80 chars) of the 108-char token, silently truncating it.\\n\\n### Logs, screenshots, and evidence\\n\\n```shell\\nGateway error log showing auth failures:\\n\\n\\n[agent/embedded] embedded run agent end: isError=true model=claude-opus-4-6 provider=anthropic error=HTTP 401 authentication_error: Invalid bearer token\\n[model-fallback/decision] model fallback decision: candidate_failed reason=auth\\n\\n\\nVerified by curl — truncated 80-char token returns 401, full 108-char token authenticates successfully:\\n\\n\\n$ # Truncated (80 chars, as stored by OpenClaw)\\n$ curl -s -X POST https://api.anthropic.com/v1/messages -H \\\"Authorization: Bearer sk-ant-oat01-FIRST80CHARS...\\\"\\n{\\\"type\\\":\\\"error\\\",\\\"error\\\":{\\\"type\\\":\\\"authentication_error\\\",\\\"message\\\":\\\"Invalid bearer token\\\"}}\\n\\n$ # Full token (108 chars)\\n$ curl -s -X POST https://api.anthropic.com/v1/messages -H \\\"Authorization: Bearer sk-ant-oat01-FULL108CHARS...\\\"\\n{\\\"type\\\":\\\"error\\\",\\\"error\\\":{\\\"type\\\":\\\"not_found_error\\\",\\\"message\\\":\\\"model: ...\\\"}}  # Auth OK, wrong model name\\n```\\n\\n### Impact and severity\\n\\nAffected: Any user pasting an Anthropic setup-token via interactive prompts on terminals where the 108-char token wraps\\nSeverity: High — completely breaks all Anthropic API calls with no clear indication of the cause\\nFrequency: 100% reproducible when terminal width causes token to wrap\\nConsequence: All Anthropic model requests fail with 401. type\\n\\nCrash (process/app exits or hangs)\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` fails to detect orphaned tool IDs produced by MiniMax (and other OpenAI-compat models) because the repair function operates on raw JSONL IDs, while the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from those IDs before sending to the API. The two ID spaces never match, so the repair passes cleanly while the API still rejects with 400.\\n\\nThis is a distinct regression from the fix in #13799 (`sanitizeToolCallIds`). That fix sanitizes IDs at serialization time, but `repairToolUseResultPairing` runs on the pre-sanitization JSONL and does its pairing check against the original IDs — so it never sees the mismatch.\\n\\n### Steps to reproduce\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\n### Step 1 — Mixed-model session\\n\\nThe session uses `haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5` for heartbeat turns and `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6` as the main model. MiniMax generates tool call IDs in the format:\\n\\n\\u003e call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1\\n\\nThese are persisted to the session JSONL verbatim.\\n\\n### Step 2 — Underscore-stripping during Anthropic serialization\\n\\nWhen OpenClaw serializes session history for the Anthropic API, tool IDs are normalized (underscores stripped). The JSONL ID `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` becomes `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the final payload.\\n\\n### Step 3 — Repair function operates on JSONL IDs, not serialized IDs\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` builds its pairing maps from raw JSONL content using `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1`. It finds a matching `toolResult` with the same ID in JSONL, concludes the pair is intact, and passes the message through.\\n\\nThe Anthropic API receives `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the `tool_use` block and looks for a matching `tool_result.tool_use_id`. It finds none and returns 400.\\n\\n### Confirmed from session JSONL\\n\\n| JSONL Entry | Role | Model | Tool ID (JSONL) |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| 31 | assistant | minimax/MiniMax-M2.5 | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` |\\n| 32 | toolResult | — | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` ✅ matched in JSONL |\\n| 110 | assistant | claude-sonnet-4-6 | `content: []`, `stopReason: \\\"error\\\"` — session bricked |\\n\\nThe repair function sees entries 31→32 as a valid pair (they match in JSONL). But the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from `tool_use.id` without applying the same normalization to `tool_result.tool_use_id`, so the API sees an unpaired `tool_use` block.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure `agents.defaults.heartbeat.model: \\\"haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\\"` (or any OpenAI-compat model generating `call_function_*`-format IDs)\\n2. Observe: Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\nReproduces reliably after ~4 turns.\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\n**Option A (preferred):** Apply the same underscore-stripping normalization inside `repairToolUseResultPairing` when building ID lookup maps, so it operates on the post-sanitization ID space.\\n\\n**Option B:** Apply normalization symmetrically to both `tool_use.id` and `tool_result.tool_use_id` during serialization, so they always match in the final payload.\\n\\n**Option C:** Add a post-serialization validation pass in the Anthropic serializer that checks every `tool_use` block has a matching `tool_result` using the final serialized IDs, injecting a synthetic error result if not.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n### Expected behavior\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` should normalize tool IDs to the same form used during Anthropic API serialization **before** performing pairing validation, so it catches mismatches the API will reject.\\n\\n\\n\\n### Actual behavior\\n\\n Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\n### OpenClaw version\\n\\n2026.3.13\\n\\n### Operating system\\n\\nLinux 6.6.87.2-microsoft-standard-WSL2 (x64)\\n\\n### Install method\\n\\nnpm global\\n\\n### Model\\n\\nminimax/MiniMax-M2.5 (heartbeat) and anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6 (primary model)\\n\\n### Provider / routing chain\\n\\nhaimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\n\\n### Additional provider/model setup details\\n\\n_No response_\\n\\n### Logs, screenshots, and evidence\\n\\n```shell\\n\\n```\\n\\n### Impact and severity\\n\\nAfter as few as four turns, session context is lost because the only way to recover is to start a new session with the /new command. type\\n\\nCrash (process/app exits or hangs)\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` fails to detect orphaned tool IDs produced by MiniMax (and other OpenAI-compat models) because the repair function operates on raw JSONL IDs, while the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from those IDs before sending to the API. The two ID spaces never match, so the repair passes cleanly while the API still rejects with 400.\\n\\nThis is a distinct regression from the fix in #13799 (`sanitizeToolCallIds`). That fix sanitizes IDs at serialization time, but `repairToolUseResultPairing` runs on the pre-sanitization JSONL and does its pairing check against the original IDs — so it never sees the mismatch.\\n\\n### Steps to reproduce\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\n### Step 1 — Mixed-model session\\n\\nThe session uses `haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5` for heartbeat turns and `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6` as the main model. MiniMax generates tool call IDs in the format:\\n\\n\\u003e call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1\\n\\nThese are persisted to the session JSONL verbatim.\\n\\n### Step 2 — Underscore-stripping during Anthropic serialization\\n\\nWhen OpenClaw serializes session history for the Anthropic API, tool IDs are normalized (underscores stripped). The JSONL ID `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` becomes `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the final payload.\\n\\n### Step 3 — Repair function operates on JSONL IDs, not serialized IDs\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` builds its pairing maps from raw JSONL content using `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1`. It finds a matching `toolResult` with the same ID in JSONL, concludes the pair is intact, and passes the message through.\\n\\nThe Anthropic API receives `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the `tool_use` block and looks for a matching `tool_result.tool_use_id`. It finds none and returns 400.\\n\\n### Confirmed from session JSONL\\n\\n| JSONL Entry | Role | Model | Tool ID (JSONL) |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| 31 | assistant | minimax/MiniMax-M2.5 | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` |\\n| 32 | toolResult | — | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` ✅ matched in JSONL |\\n| 110 | assistant | claude-sonnet-4-6 | `content: []`, `stopReason: \\\"error\\\"` — session bricked |\\n\\nThe repair function sees entries 31→32 as a valid pair (they match in JSONL). But the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from `tool_use.id` without applying the same normalization to `tool_result.tool_use_id`, so the API sees an unpaired `tool_use` block.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure `agents.defaults.heartbeat.model: \\\"haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\\"` (or any OpenAI-compat model generating `call_function_*`-format IDs)\\n2. Trigger a heartbeat that causes MiniMax to make tool calls (e.g. a clawflows scheduler run)\\n3. Send a message to the main session routing to `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6`\\n4. Observe: Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\nReproduces reliably after ~4 turns.\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\n**Option A (preferred):** Apply the same underscore-stripping normalization inside `repairToolUseResultPairing` when building ID lookup maps, so it operates on the post-sanitization ID space.\\n\\n**Option B:** Apply normalization symmetrically to both `tool_use.id` and `tool_result.tool_use_id` during serialization, so they always match in the final payload.\\n\\n**Option C:** Add a post-serialization validation pass in the Anthropic serializer that checks every `tool_use` block has a matching `tool_result` using the final serialized IDs, injecting a synthetic error result if not.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n### Expected behavior\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` should normalize tool IDs to the same form used during Anthropic API serialization **before** performing pairing validation, so it catches mismatches the API will reject.\\n\\n\\n\\n### Actual behavior\\n\\n Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\n### OpenClaw version\\n\\n2026.3.13\\n\\n### Operating system\\n\\nLinux 6.6.87.2-microsoft-standard-WSL2 (x64)\\n\\n### Install method\\n\\nnpm global\\n\\n### Model\\n\\nminimax/MiniMax-M2.5 (heartbeat) and anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6 (primary model)\\n\\n### Provider / routing chain\\n\\nhaimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\n\\n### Additional provider/model setup details\\n\\n_No response_\\n\\n### Logs, screenshots, and evidence\\n\\n```shell\\n\\n```\\n\\n### Impact and severity\\n\\nAfter as few as four turns, session context is lost because the only way to recover is to start a new session with the /new command.
